            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Room-temp. sodium-ion batteries are of great interest for high-energy-d. energy storage systems because of low-cost and natural abundance of sodium.  Here, we report a novel phosphorus/graphene nanosheet hybrid as a high-performance anode for sodium-ion batteries through facile ball milling of red phosphorus and graphene stacks.  The graphene stacks are mech. exfoliated to nanosheets that chem. bond with the surfaces of phosphorus particles.  This chem. bonding can facilitate robust and intimate contact between phosphorus and graphene nanosheets, and the graphene at the particle surfaces can help maintain elec. contact and stabilize the solid electrolyte interphase upon the large vol. change of phosphorus during cycling.  As a result, the phosphorus/graphene nanosheet hybrid nanostructured anode delivers a high reversible capacity of 2077 mA-h/g with excellent cycling stability (1700 mA-h/g after 60 cycles) and high coulombic efficiency (&gt;98%).  This simple synthesis approach and unique nanostructure can potentially be applied to other phosphorus-based alloy anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrK8W0lUv46brVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljcLLiWqlB6vA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVens77N&amp;md5=a7b5dd550d23d77899dcd28546675af8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1021/ja3091438"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goodenough, J. B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, K. S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Li-Ion Rechargeable Battery: A Perspective</span>. <i>J. Am. Chem.                 10.1021/ja3091438</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D135%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D1167-1176%26journal%3DJ.%2BAm.%2BChem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DJ.%2BB.%2BGoodenough%26author%3DK.%2BS.%2BPark%26title%3DThe%2BLi-Ion%2BRechargeable%2BBattery%253A%2BA%2BPerspective%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fja3091438&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.8b04075&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fja3091438&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Li-Ion Rechargeable Battery: A Perspective</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Goodenough, John B.; Park, Kyu-Sung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">135</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1167-1176</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Each cell of a battery stores elec. energy as chem. energy in two electrodes, a reductant (anode) and an oxidant (cathode), sepd. by an electrolyte that transfers the ionic component of the chem. reaction inside the cell and forces the electronic component outside the battery.  The output on discharge is an external electronic current I at a voltage V for a time Δt.  The chem. reaction of a rechargeable battery must be reversible on the application of a charging I and V.  Crit. parameters of a rechargeable battery are safety, d. of energy that can be stored at a specific power input and retrieved at a specific power output, cycle and shelf life, storage efficiency, and cost of fabrication.  Conventional ambient-temp. rechargeable batteries have solid electrodes and a liq. electrolyte.  The pos. electrode (cathode) consists of a host framework into which the mobile (working) cation is inserted reversibly over a finite solid-soln. range.  The solid-soln. range, which is reduced at higher current by the rate of transfer of the working ion across electrode/electrolyte interfaces and within a host, limits the amt. of charge per electrode formula unit that can be transferred over the time Δt = Δt(I).  Moreover, the difference between energies of the LUMO and the HOMO of the electrolyte, i.e., electrolyte window, dets. the max. voltage for a long shelf and cycle life.  The max. stable voltage with an aq. electrolyte is 1.5 V; the Li-ion rechargeable battery uses an org. electrolyte with a larger window, which increase the d. of stored energy for a given Δt.  Anode or cathode electrochem. potentials outside the electrolyte window can increase V, but they require formation of a passivating surface layer that must be permeable to Li+ and capable of adapting rapidly to the changing electrode surface area as the electrode changes vol. during cycling.  A passivating surface layer adds to the impedance of the Li+ transfer across the electrode/electrolyte interface and lowers the cycle life of a battery cell.  Moreover, formation of a passivation layer on the anode robs Li from the cathode irreversibly on an initial charge, further lowering the reversible Δt.  These problems plus the cost of quality control of manufg. plague development of Li-ion rechargeable batteries that can compete with the internal combustion engine for powering elec. cars and that can provide the needed low-cost storage of elec. energy generated by renewable wind and/or solar energy.  Chemists are contributing to incremental improvements of the conventional strategy by investigating and controlling electrode passivation layers, improving the rate of Li+ transfer across electrode/electrolyte interfaces, identifying electrolytes with larger windows while retaining a Li+ cond. σLi &gt; 10-3 S cm-1, synthesizing electrode morphologies that reduce the size of the active particles while pinning them on current collectors of large surface area accessible by the electrolyte, lowering the cost of cell fabrication, designing displacement-reaction anodes of higher capacity that allow a safe, fast charge, and designing alternative cathode hosts.  However, new strategies are needed for batteries that go beyond powering hand-held devices, such as using electrode hosts with two-electron redox centers; replacing the cathode hosts by materials that undergo displacement reactions (e.g. sulfur) by liq. cathodes that may contain flow-through redox mols., or by catalysts for air cathodes; and developing a Li+ solid electrolyte separator membrane that allows an org. and aq. liq. electrolyte on the anode and cathode sides, resp.  Opportunities exist for the chemist to bring together oxide and polymer or graphene chem. in imaginative morphologies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqqKg_SkQGkZrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljsPVfEO-I2FA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXktFSisw%253D%253D&amp;md5=9b3d655905f4b3dc188e98f8370452df</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201306314"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, B.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A SnS2-RGO composite with excellent electrochem. performance was prepd. as the anode of sodium ion batteries.  The SnS2-RGO electrode demonstrated a high charge specific capacity (630 mAh g-1 at 0.2 A g-1), good rate performance (544 mAh g-1 at 2 A g-1) and long cycle-life (500 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 for 400 cycles).                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent research progress on iron- and manganese-based positive electrode materials for rechargeable sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science and Technology of Advanced Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Large-scale high-energy batteries with electrode materials made from the Earth-abundant elements are needed to achieve sustainable energy development.  On the basis of material abundance, rechargeable sodium batteries with iron- and manganese-based pos. electrode materials are the ideal candidates for large-scale batteries.  In this review, iron- and manganese-based electrode materials, oxides, phosphates, fluorides, etc., as pos. electrodes for rechargeable sodium batteries are reviewed.  Iron and manganese compds. with sodium ions provide high structural flexibility.  Two layered polymorphs, O3- and P2-type layered structures, show different electrode performance in Na cells related to the different phase transition and sodium migration processes on sodium extn./insertion.  Similar to layered oxides, iron/manganese phosphates and pyrophosphates also provide the different framework structures, which are used as sodium insertion host materials.  Electrode performance and reaction mechanisms of the iron- and manganese-based electrode materials in Na cells are described and the similarities and differences with lithium counterparts are also discussed.  Together with these results, the possibility of the high-energy battery system with electrode materials made from only Earth-abundant elements is reviewed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGofxbe5Y3n5JLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljsPVfEO-I2FA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFKru7jE&amp;md5=4883e3ff3fa350ed4ccd8768ae2868ae</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1039/C7EE00102A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bian, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Controlled Red Phosphorus@Ni-P Core@Shell Nanostructure as An Ultralong Cycle-Life and Superior High-Rate Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A controlled red phosphorus@Ni-P core@shell nanostructure as an ultralong cycle-life and superior high-rate anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Shuai; Feng, Jinkui; Bian, Xiufang; Liu, Jie; Xu, Hui; An, Yongling</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), a potential alternative to lithium ion batteries (LIBs), have attracted remarkable attention recently due to the natural abundance and low-cost of sodium.  Here, we have presented a comprehensive study on combining electroless deposition with chem. dealloying to control the shell thickness and compn. of a red phosphorus (RP)@Ni-P core@shell nanostructure as a high performance anode for SIBs.  For the first time depending on regulating the dealloying time (1 h, 4 h, 8 h, 10 h and 20 h) of RP@Ni-P synthesized by electroless deposition of Ni on RP, 1 h RP@Ni-P, 4 h RP@Ni-P, 8 h RP@Ni-P, 10 h RP@Ni-P and 20 h RP@Ni-P with different shell thicknesses and compns. were prepd.  The in situ generated Ni2P on RP particle surfaces can facilitate intimate contact between RP and a mech. strong amorphous Ni-P outer shell with a high electronic cond., which ensures strong electrode structural integrity, a stable solid electrolyte interphase and ultra-fast electronic transport.  As a result, the 8 h RP@Ni-P composite presents a super high capacity (1256.2 mA h gcomposite-1 after 200 cycles at 260 mA gcomposite-1), superior rate capability (491 mA h gcomposite-1 at 5200 mA gcomposite-1) and unprecedented ultralong cycle-life at 5000 mA gcomposite-1 for an RP-based SIB anode (409.1 mA h gcomposite-1 after 2000 cycles).  This simple scalable synthesis approach will provide a new strategy for the optimization of core@shell nanostructures, paving the way for mass prodn. of high performance electrodes for SIBs and other energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoVRwOrxeWHubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljsPVfEO-I2FA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXlsVyqurg%253D&amp;md5=5a9d70a9ec338f9b2bf0d110723db337</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1039/C5EE03699B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bian, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Morphology-Controlled Synthesis of A Nanoporous-Antimony Anode for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The morphology-controlled synthesis of a nanoporous-antimony anode for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Shuai; Feng, Jinkui; Bian, Xiufang; Liu, Jie; Xu, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We have presented a comprehensive study of using chem. dealloying methods to control the morphol. of nanoporous-antimony (NP-Sb) and the size of Sb particles.  For the first time, depending on the regulation of the Al-Sb alloy compn., coral-like NP-Sb (NP-Sb70), honeycomb-like NP-Sb (NP-Sb80) and Sb particles (Sb10, Sb30 and Sb45) with different sizes were prepd. through chem. dealloying of Al30Sb70, Al20Sb80, Al90Sb10, Al70Sb30 and Al55Sb45 (at%) alloy ribbon precursors resp., a top-down process.  The NP-Sb70 delivered a high capacity of 573.8 mA h g-1 after 200 cycles at a rate of 100 mA g-1 with good rate capability as anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  The excellent electrochem. performance is because of its innovative electrode design, which ensures strong structural integrity, high sodium ion accessibility, and fast electrode transport.  This scalable strategy shall pave the way for the mass prodn. of large-capacity electrodes for SIBs and other energy storage systems, providing new guidelines for the optimization of the synthesis of nanostructures.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqGZBR5siNySrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4j8eGV7Vjlw"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1021/acs.nanolett.5b03903</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D16%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D1546-1553%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26author%3DW.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.%2BYang%26author%3DM.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BJiang%26author%3DX.%2BWei%26author%3DX.%2BZhong%26author%3DL.%2BGu%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26title%3DAmorphous%2BRed%2BPhosphorus%2BEmbedded%2Bin%2BHighly%2BOrdered%2BMesoporous%2BCarbon%2Bwith%2BSuperior%2BLithium%2Band%2BSodium%2BStorage%2BCapacity%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.nanolett.5b03903&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.8b04075&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.5b03903&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous Red Phosphorus Embedded in Highly Ordered Mesoporous Carbon with Superior Lithium and Sodium Storage Capacity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Weihan; Yang, Zhenzhong; Li, Minsi; Jiang, Yu; Wei, Xiang; Zhong, Xiongwu; Gu, Lin; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1546-1553</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus (P) have been considered as one of the most promising anode material for both lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (NIBs), because of its high theor. capacity.  However, natural insulating property and the large vol. expansion of red P during cycling lead to poor cyclability and low rate performance, which prevents its practical application.  Here, the lithium storage and sodium storage performance of red P is significantly improved by confining nanosized amorphous red P into the mesoporous carbon matrix (P@CMK-3) using a vaporization-condensation-conversion process.  The P@CMK-3 shows a high reversible specific capacity of ∼2250 mA h g-1 based on the mass of red P at 0.25 C (∼971 mA h g-1 based on the composite), excellent rate performance of 1598 and 624 mA h g-1 based on the mass of red P at 6.1 and 12 C, resp. (562 and 228 mA h g-1 based on the mass of the composite at 6.1 and 12 C, resp.), and significantly enhanced cycle life of 1150 mA h g-1 based on the mass of red P at 5 C (500 mA h g-1 based on the mass of the composite) after 1000 cycles for LIBs.  For Na ions, it also displays a reversible capacity of 1020 mA h g-1 based on the mass of red P (370 mA h g-1 based on the mass of the composite) after 210 cycles at 5C.  The significantly improved electrochem. performance could be attributed to the unique structure that combines a variety of advantages: easy access of electrolyte to the open channel structure, short transport path of ions through carbon toward the red P, and high ionic and electronic cond.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpOPPN6BIYNN7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4j8eGV7Vjlw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Red Phosphorus Nanodots on Reduced Graphene Oxide as a Flexible and Ultra-Fast Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yihang; Zhang, Anyi; Shen, Chenfei; Liu, Qingzhou; Cao, Xuan; Ma, Yuqiang; Chen, Liang; Lau, Christian; Chen, Tian-Chi; Wei, Fei; Zhou, Chongwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5530-5537</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries offer an attractive option for potential low cost and large scale energy storage due to the earth abundance of Na.  Red P is considered as a high capacity anode for Na-ion batteries with a theor. capacity of 2596 mA-h/g.  However, similar to Si in Li-ion batteries, several limitations, such as large vol. expansion upon sodiation/desodiation and low electronic conductance, have limited the performance of red P anodes.  To address the above challenges, the authors have developed a method to deposit red P nanodots densely and uniformly onto reduced graphene oxide sheets (P@RGO) to minimize the Na ion diffusion length and the sodiation/desodiation stresses, and the RGO network also serves as electron pathway and creates free space to accommodate the vol. variation of P particles.  The resulted P@RGO flexible anode achieved 1165.4, 510.6, and 135.3 mA-h/g specific charge capacity at 159.4, 31878.9, and 47818.3 mA/g charge/discharge c.d. in rate capability test, and a 914 mA-h/g capacity after 300 deep cycles in cycling stability test at 1593.9 mA/g c.d., which marks a significant performance improvement for red P anodes for Na-ion chem. and flexible power sources for wearable electronics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo9mlp0D8us-rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4j8eGV7Vjlw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Simply mixed commercial red phosphorus and carbon nanotube composite with exceptionally reversible sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wei-Jie; Chou, Shu-Lei; Wang, Jia-Zhao; Liu, Hua-Kun; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been given intense attention because they are the most promising alternative to lithium ion batteries for application in renewable power stations and smart grid, owing to their low cost, their abundant natural resources, and the similar chem. of sodium and lithium.  Elemental phosphorus (P) is the most promising anode materials for SIBs with the highest theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1, but the com. available red phosphorus cannot react with Na reversibly.  Here, we report that simply hand-grinding com. microsized red phosphorus and carbon nanotubes (CNTs) can deliver a reversible capacity of 1675 mA h g-1 for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), with capacity retention of 76.6% over 10 cycles.  Our results suggest that the simply mixed com. red phosphorus and CNTs would be a promising anode candidate for SIBs with a high capacity and low cost.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoXaIaGjScJ9bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4j8eGV7Vjlw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhslSgtb7F&amp;md5=0d930b4524af251e6376a18cb67d5e91</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1149/2.0151501jes"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NaV<sub>6</sub>O<sub>15</sub> Nanoflakes with Good Cycling Stability as A Cathode for Sodium Ion Battery</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A multifunctional 3.5 V iron-based phosphate cathode for rechargeable batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ellis, B.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In the search for new pos.-electrode materials for lithium-ion batteries, recent research has focused on nanostructured lithium transition-metal phosphates that exhibit desirable properties such as high energy storage capacity combined with electrochem. stability.  Only one member of this class-the olivine LiFePO4 (ref. 3)-has risen to prominence so far, owing to its other characteristics, which include low cost, low environmental impact and safety.  These are crit. for large-capacity systems such as plug-in hybrid elec. vehicles.  Nonetheless, olivine has some inherent shortcomings, including 1-dimensional lithium-ion transport and a two-phase redox reaction that together limit the mobility of the phase boundary.  Thus, nanocrystallites are key to enable fast rate behavior.  Also probably the long-term economic viability of large-scale Li-ion energy storage systems could be ultimately limited by global lithium reserves, although this remains speculative at present.  Here, the authors report on a sodium/lithium iron phosphate, A2FePO4F (A = Na, Li), that could serve as a cathode in either Li-ion or Na-ion cells.  Also, it possesses facile two-dimensional pathways for Li+ transport, and the structural changes on redn.-oxidn. are minimal.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, NaV3O8 nanowires are proposed as a novel cathode for a Na-ion battery for the first time.  The as-prepd. nanowires are characterized well by X-ray diffraction (XRD), Fourier transform IR (FT-IR) spectra, thermogravimetry (TG), XPS, and transmission electron microscopy (TEM).  Sodium insertion/extn. properties of as-prepd. nanowires with or without thermal treatment are compared.  It is found that thermal treatment could remove some crystal water in the host, resulting in a contracted crystal vol.  In comparison with the untreated sample, although the reversible discharge capacity of annealed NaV3O8·xH2O nanowires is decreased from 169.6 mA h g-1 to 145.8 mA h g-1 when cycled at 10 mA g-1, it shows good capacity retention of ca. 91.1% after 50 cycles, much higher than that (51.9%) of the untreated sample.  Annealed NaV3O8 nanowires exhibit much better cycling stability and charge-discharge plateaus during the Na-ion insertion/extn. processes, which should be attributed to the contracted crystal vol. and the increased crystallinity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqezOy3BTgQGLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0licvoSKBwEDWg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intercalation of Bi nanoparticles into graphite results in an ultra-fast and ultra-stable anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Ji; Fan, Xiulin; Ji, Xiao; Gao, Tao; Hou, Singyuk; Zhou, Xiuquan; Wang, Luning; Wang, Fei; Yang, Chongyin; Chen, Long; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1218-1225</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been revived as important alternative energy storage devices for large-scale energy storage, which requires SIBs to have a long cycling life and high power d.  However, the scarcity of suitable anode materials hinders their application.  Herein, we report a bismuth intercalated graphite (Bi@Graphite) anode material, which is substantially different from the previously reported metal@Graphene.  In Bi@Graphite, the Bi nanoparticles between graphite interlayers enhance the capacity, while the graphite sheath provides a robust fast electronic connection for long cycling stability.  The Bi@Graphite possesses a safe av. storage potential of approx. 0.5 V vs.  Na/Na+, delivers a capacity of ∼160 mA h g-1 at 1C (160 mA g-1), exhibits outstanding cycling stability (ca. 90% capacity retention for 10 000 cycles at 20C), and can maintain 70% capacity at 300C (∼110 mA h g-1 at 48 A g-1), which is equiv. to full charge/discharge in 12 s.  Bi@Graphite demonstrates the highest rate-capability ever reported among all anodes for SIBs.  Detailed characterization results indicate that the unique Bi nanoparticle-in-graphite structure and the fast kinetics of ether co-intercalation into graphite are responsible for these significant improvements, which could translate into SIBs with excellent power densities.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoSO-lUIYzLkbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0licvoSKBwEDWg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXmtVCisrs%253D&amp;md5=fad06b243c2fb803c4692029376e7f13</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1080/00018738100101367"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dresselhaus, M.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemical performance of porous carbon/tin composite anodes for sodium-ion and lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Yunhua; Zhu, Yujie; Liu, Yihang; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. performance of mesoporous carbon (C)/tin (Sn) anodes in Na-ion and Li-ion batteries is systematically investigated.  The mesoporous C/Sn anodes in a Na-ion battery shows similar cycling stability but lower capacity and poorer rate capability than that in a Li-ion battery.  The desodiation potentials of Sn anodes are approx. 0.21 V lower than delithiation potentials.  The low capacity and poor rate capability of C/Sn anode in Na-ion batteries is mainly due to the large Na-ion size, resulting in slow Na-ion diffusion and large vol. change of porous C/Sn composite anode during alloy/dealloy reactions.  Understanding of the reaction mechanism between Sn and Na ions will provide insight towards exploring and designing new alloy-based anode materials for Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqL8pwZXJa53LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0licvoSKBwEDWg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhsFKhtr8%253D&amp;md5=7fba4efb710816f1ca877f0494169a46</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1039/c2cc17129e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kovarik, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity, Reversible Alloying Reactions in SnSb/C Nanocomposites for Na-Ion Battery Applications</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phosphorus electrodes in sodium cells: small volume expansion by sodiation and the surface-stabilization mechanism in aprotic solvent</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Matsuura, Yuta; Ishikawa, Toru; Kuze, Satoru; Son, Jin-Young; Cui, Yi-Tao; Oji, Hiroshi; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrode performance of amorphous phosphorus in aprotic Na cells is examd.  Amorphous phosphorus is electrochem. reduced in the Na cells with a three-electron redox process, crystg. into Na3P.  Na-P bonds in Na3P have high covalent characteristics.  Therefore, the molar volume of Na in Na3P is anomalously small in comparison to other Na-metal alloys that have been used as neg. electrode materials.  The theor. volumetric capacity, calcd. at full vol. expansion of amorphous phosphorus electrodes through sodiation, is expected to be 27% larger than that of metallic sodium.  However, exptl., it is found that severe electrolyte decompn. results in insufficient reversibility of the electrode materials, owing to the highly reactive Na3P surface.  Electrode reversibility is successfully improved by utilizing an electrolyte additive, fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC).  The surface chem. of phosphorus in the aprotic solvent with sodium salts is examd. by hard/soft XPS (PES).  PES studies reveal that FEC effectively stabilizes the solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI), contg. monovalent phosphorus species and sodium fluoride, and thus electrolyte decompn. is partly suppressed by the relatively stable SEI formed on the surface of phosphorus particles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqpBUNr-VIkQrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljuxw9NY2KNrA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhslWisrvK&amp;md5=ed8f5cf0ca24d4e057ca230d2c04e29c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201209689"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity and Rate Capability of Amorphous Phosphorus for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew. The a-P/C composite displayed a surprisingly high sodium ion storage capacity of 1764 mA-h/g and considerable cyclability over 100 cycles.  This is the first time such a high capacity and rate capability has been reported for phosphorus anode materials.  Combining with the natural abundance and environmental friendliness of phosphorus, the a-P/C composite offers promise as a high capacity and high rate anodic material for the next generation of sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGplgZHrXYfuSrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljuxw9NY2KNrA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXksVOhtbs%253D&amp;md5=3c2790414de1a6ac184ca3fabe1e48aa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201204877"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, N.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Advanced Sodium Ion Battery Anode Constructed via Chemical Bonding between Phosphorus, Carbon Nanotube, and Cross-Linked Polymer Binder</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song, Jiangxuan; Yu, Zhaoxin; Gordin, Mikhail L.; Li, Xiaolin; Peng, Huisheng; Wang, Donghai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Maintaining structural stability is a great challenge for high-capacity conversion electrodes with large vol. change but is necessary for the development of high-energy-d., long-cycling batteries.  Here, a stable phosphorus anode is reported for sodium ion batteries by the synergistic use of chem. bonded phosphorus-carbon nanotube (P-CNT) hybrid and cross-linked polymer binder.  The P-CNT hybrid was synthesized through ball-milling of red phosphorus and carboxylic group functionalized carbon nanotubes.  The P-O-C bonds formed in this process help maintain contact between phosphorus and CNTs, leading to a durable hybrid.  In addn., cross-linked CM-cellulose-citric acid binder was used to form a robust electrode.  As a result, this anode delivers a stable cycling capacity of 1586.2 mAh/g after 100 cycles, along with high initial Coulombic efficiency of 84.7% and subsequent cycling efficiency of ∼99%.  The unique electrode framework through chem. bonding strategy reported here is potentially inspirable for other electrode materials with large vol. change in use.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoS4Pq1G8HaQrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljuxw9NY2KNrA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslWjsb7E&amp;md5=7aa0ddefccdd71c9a74a5848ed1dbe6e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1021/nl403053v"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Simply Mixed Commercial Red Phosphorus and Carbon Nanotube Composite with Exceptionally Reversible Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Nano Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">5480</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5484</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Simply mixed commercial red phosphorus and carbon nanotube composite with exceptionally reversible sodium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Wei-Jie; Chou, Shu-Lei; Wang, Jia-Zhao; Liu, Hua-Kun; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been given intense attention because they are the most promising alternative to lithium ion batteries for application in renewable power stations and smart grid, owing to their low cost, their abundant natural resources, and the similar chem. of sodium and lithium.  Elemental phosphorus (P) is the most promising anode materials for SIBs with the highest theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1, but the com. available red phosphorus cannot react with Na reversibly.  Here, we report that simply hand-grinding com. microsized red phosphorus and carbon nanotubes (CNTs) can deliver a reversible capacity of 1675 mA h g-1 for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), with capacity retention of 76.6% over 10 cycles.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Red Phosphorus-Single-Walled Carbon Nanotube Composite as a Superior Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Yujie; Wen, Yang; Fan, Xiulin; Gao, Tao; Han, Fudong; Luo, Chao; Liou, Sz-Chian; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered as a top alternative to Li ion batteries due to the earth abundance and low cost of Na compared with Li.  Among all proposed anode materials for SIBs, red P is a very promising candidate because it has the highest theor. capacity (∼2600 mA-h g-1).  A red P-single-walled C nanotube (denoted as red P-SWCNT) composite, in which red P is uniformly distributed between tangled SWCNTs bundles, is fabricated by a modified vaporization-condensation method.  Benefiting from the nondestructive prepn. process, the highly conductive and mech. strong SWCNT network is preserved, which enhances the cond. of the composite and stabilizes the solid electrolyte interphase.  As a result, the red P-SWCNT composite presents a high overall Na storage capacity (∼700 mA-h g-1composite at 50 mA/gcomposite), fast rate capability (∼300 mA-h g-1composite at 2000 mA/gcomposite), and stable long-term cycling performance with 80% capacity retention after 2000 sodiation-desodiation cycles.  The red P-SWCNT composite fabricated by the vaporization-condensation method significantly extends the cycling stability of P/C composite from current ∼100 cycles to ∼2000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqd3GxgIxmfmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljuxw9NY2KNrA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXjvVOhs7c%253D&amp;md5=6ba87307633bf69051e0eb4e034c85a8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201601037"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Integrated Carbon/Red Phosphorus/Graphene Aerogel 3D Architecture <i>via</i> Advanced Vapor-Redistribution for High-Energy Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanoporous germanium as high-capacity lithium-ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Shuai; Feng, Jinkui; Bian, Xiufang; Qian, Yitai; Liu, Jie; Xu, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

                        cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanoengineering to Achieve High Sodium Storage: A Case Study of Carbon Coated Hierarchical Nanoporous TiO2 Microfibers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang Nu; Gao Yuan; Liu Kai; Zhao Yong; Jiang Lei; Wang Yun-Xiao; Lai Weihong; Hu Yemin; Chou Shu-Lei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1600013</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanoengineering of electrode materials can directly facilitate sodium ion accessibility and transport, thus enhancing electrochemical performance in sodium ion batteries.  Here, highly sodium-accessible carbon coated nanoporous TiO2 microfibers have been synthesised via the facile electrospinning technique which can deliver an enhanced capacity of ≈167 mAh g(-1) after 450 cycles at current density of 50 mA g(-1) and retain a capacity of ≈71 mAh g(-1) at the high current rate of 1 A g(-1).  With the benefits of their porous structure, thin TiO2 inner walls, and the introduction of conductive carbon, the nanoporous TiO2/C microfibers exhibit high ion accessibility, fast Na ion transport, and fast electron transport, thereby leading to the excellent Na-storage properties presented here.  Nanostructuring is proven to be a fruitful strategy that can alleviate the reliance on materials' intrinsic nature; and the electrospinning technique is versatile and cost-effective for the fabrication of such an effective nanoporous microfiber structure.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcRu2RD154rBGwyMywPm6HgQfW6udTcc2eZfSVgXzicFCLntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC2snjsFGnsQ%253D%253D&amp;md5=ca63388cbe77319e18a8708089204e9a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1021/nl501692p"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Raju, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rains, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gates, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stickle, W.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Superior Cathode of Sodium-Ion Batteries: Orthorhombic V2O5 Nanoparticles Generated in Nanoporous Carbon by Ambient Hydrolysis Deposition</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Raju, Vadivukarasi; Rains, Jordan; Gates, Cooper; Luo, Wei; Wang, Xingfeng; Stickle, William F.; Stucky, Galen D.; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">For the first time, we demonstrate that orthorhombic V2O5 can exhibit superior electrochem. performance in sodium ion batteries when uniformly coated inside nanoporous carbon.  The encapsulated V2O5 shows a specific capacity as high as 276 mAh/g, while the whole nanocomposite exhibits a capacity of 170 mAh/g.  The V2O5/C composite was fabricated by a novel ambient hydrolysis deposition that features sequential water vapor adsorption in nanoporous carbon, followed by a hydrolysis reaction, exclusively inside the nanopores.  The unique structure of the nanocomposite significantly enhances the capacity as well as the rate performance of orthorhombic V2O5 where the composite retains a capacity of over 90 mAh/g at a current rate of 640 mA/g.  Furthermore, by calcg., we also revealed that a large portion of the sodium-ion storage, particularly at high current rates, is due to the V2O5 pseudocapacitance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrAc4ZtbEuUc7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljFZko6Jtmoag"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXpvFCnsbY%253D&amp;md5=396440b0fdbdbc5738bd8355b702938b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1246/cl.161185"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oro, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Urita, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Moriguchi, I.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanospace-Controlled SnO<sub>2</sub>/Nanoporous Carbon Composite as A High-Performance Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanospace-controlled SnO2/nanoporous carbon composite as a high-performance anode for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Oro, Shinji; Urita, Koki; Moriguchi, Isamu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry Letters</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Chemical Society of Japan</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. performance of SnO2 as an anode material for sodium ion batteries was greatly enhanced by embedding SnO2 nanocrystallites preferentially in the porous carbon.  The appropriate loading of SnO2 (e.g., 62 wt%) so as to provide enough reaction space resulted in a high capacity retention of 84% in the 30th cycle and a high capacity of 387mAh g-1.  It was demonstrated by electrochem. impedance spectroscopy that the enhancement was due to lowering of the charge-transfer resistance in the nanospace-controlled composite.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp3Vib2tVC1ibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljFZko6Jtmoag"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtVGrtb%252FO&amp;md5=efe64e14949863296aa97b0254ea3a40</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.04.032"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Graphene-Based Nano-Materials for Lithium–Sulfur Battery and Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>15</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">379</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">405</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene-based nano-materials for lithium-sulfur battery and sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Songping; Ge, Rongyun; Lu, Mingjia; Xu, Rui; Zhang, Zhen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene-based nano-materials have provided an opportunity for next-generation energy storage device, particularly for lithium-sulfur battery and sodium-ion battery (SIB), due to their unique properties.  This review comprehensively summarizes the present achievements and the latest progress of inorg. nano-materials/graphene composites as the electrode materials for Li-S battery and SIBs.  Electrochem. principles, performances and key obstructions of graphene-based materials in the actual application are considered.  This review gathers and classifies updated knowledge about Li-S battery and SIB nanomaterials related to graphene, with the aim of offering a wide view of those systems.  It is concluded that cost-effective SIBs and Li-S battery are promising next-generation battery candidates in the near future, but require further investigation and improvement to deal with some crit. scientific issues.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGquh6fB9vQzeLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljjIJrrhvlD-A"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solution Synthesis of Iodine-Doped Red Phosphorus Nanoparticles for Lithium-Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chang, Wei-Chung; Tseng, Kuan-Wei; Tuan, Hsing-Yu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1240-1247</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus (RP) is a promising anode material for lithium-ion batteries due to its earth abundance and a high theor. capacity of 2596 mA h g-1.  Although RP-based anodes for lithium-ion batteries have been reported, they were all in the form of carbon-P composites, including P-graphene, P-graphite, P-carbon nanotubes (CNTs), and P-carbon black, to improve P's extremely low cond. and large vol. change during cycling process.  Here, we report the large-scale synthesis of red phosphorus nanoparticles (RPNPs) with sizes ranging from 100 to 200 nm by reacting PI3 with ethylene glycol in the presence of cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB) in ambient environment.  Unlike the insulator behavior of com. RP (cond. of &lt;10 -12 S m-1), the cond. of RPNPs is between 2.62 × 10-3 and 1.81 × 10-2 S m-1, which is close to that of semiconductor germanium (1.02 × 10-2 S m-1), and 2 orders of magnitude higher than silicon (5.35 × 10-4 S m-1).  Around 3-5 wt % of iodine-doping was found in RPNPs, which was speculated as the key to significantly improve the cond. of RPNPs.  The significantly improved cond. of RPNPs and their uniform colloidal nanostructures enable them to be used solely as active materials for LIBs anodes.  The RPNPs electrodes exhibit a high specific capacity of 1700 mA h g-1 (0.2 C after 100 cycles, 1 C = 2000 mA g-1), long cycling life (∼900 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1 C), and outstanding rate capability (175 mA h g-1 at the charge c.d. of 120 A g-1, 60 C).  Moreover, as a proof-of-concept example, pouch-type full cells using RPNPs anodes and Li(Ni0.5Co0.3Mn0.2)O2 (NCM-532) cathodes were assembled to show their practical uses.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqZ2BwgPjhTMrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljjIJrrhvlD-A"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mechanically Tough Large-Area Hierarchical Porous Graphene Films for High-Performance Flexible Supercapacitor Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Zhiyuan; Liao, Cailian; Han, Weihua; Wang, Xiaogong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We report a novel method developed to feasibly fabricate flexible large-area hierarchical porous graphenefilms by utilizing GO hydrogel as the initial feedstock.  The GO hydrogel films were prepd. by the convenient blade-casting technique and then reduced by hydroiodic acid/acetic acid (HI/HAc) under a low temp.  For the first time, the current study demonstrates that, in contrast to the poor processability of aq. GO dispersions, viscous GO hydrogel is a highly processable material and can be readily processed to films with desired sizes and shapes.  After fabricating to thin films with suitable sizes, mech. tough graphene electrodes with macroporous/mesoporous structures are feasibly obtained by the redn. of the stable GO hydrogel with HI/HAc.  A flexible supercapacitor fabricated with RGO electrodes exhibits high areal specific capacitance (71.0 mF/cm2 at 1 mA /cm2 ), excellent rate performance (79.0% retention at 100 mA/cm2), and long cycle life (98.3% retention after 5000 cycles). Astonishingly, the flexible supercapacitor prepd. with the electrodes can be bent to arbitrary angles (even 180γ) with an almost negligible capacity loss.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqHdFCJVgiVJ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljjIJrrhvlD-A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFWjsrrN&amp;md5=16d0676a130d027848bf1591afbc3277</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1016/j.snb.2017.05.060"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrasensitive NO<sub>2</sub> Gas Sensing Based on RGO/MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanocomposite Film at Low Temperature</span>. <i>Sens.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrasensitive NO2 gas sensing based on rGO/MoS2 nanocomposite film at low temperature</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Yong; Liu, Guoqing; Zhu, Xiangyi; Guo, Yongcai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Sensors and Actuators, B: Chemical</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">251</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this paper, both reduced graphene oxide (rGO) and rGO/molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) composite films serving as sensing layers were prepd. for nitrogen dioxide (NO2) gas detection at low operation temp., wherein multiple characterization techniques contg. TEM, XRD, XPS and Raman were employed.  The exptl. results showed that rGO/MoS2 composite film possessed a larger exposure area, more sorption sites and a mass of p-n heterojunctions, thereby resulting in a sensing response of 59.8% toward 2 ppm NO2 at 60 °C (optimal operation temp.), which was nearly 200% enhanced in comparison with bare rGO one.  Furthermore, we investigated the role of rGO or MoS2 material in the sensing performance as well as the effect of different MoS2 introduction manners.  Apart from these, relative humidity was found to pose a small interfering impact on NO2 response, while long-term stability on exposure to 120 ppb NO2 revealed a small response decay after several weeks.  Moreover, the composites showed an excellent selectivity toward NO2 gas against other interfering gas species.  Through further exploration of ppb-level NO2 detection, the detection limit was calcd. to be as low as 5.7 ppb.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrJJC0VM_-LTLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljjIJrrhvlD-A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXot1aht74%253D&amp;md5=cad22b628f9214643a122136cf22efd8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2010.02.001"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Murali, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stoller, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Velamakanni, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Piner, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ruoff, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Microwave Assisted Exfoliation and Reduction of Graphite Oxide for Ultracapacitors</span>. <i>Carbon</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2010</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>48</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2118</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2122</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors report a simple yet versatile method to simultaneously achieve the exfoliation and redn. of graphite oxide.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The reduction of graphene oxide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pei, Songfeng; Cheng, Hui-Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">50</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3210-3228</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Graphene has attracted great interest for its excellent mech., elec., thermal and optical properties.  It can be produced by micro-mech. exfoliation of highly ordered pyrolytic graphite, epitaxial growth, CVD, and the redn. of graphene oxide (GO).  The 1st 3 methods can produce graphene with a relatively perfect structure and excellent properties, but in comparison, GO has 2 important characteristics: (a) it can be produced using inexpensive graphite as raw material by cost-effective chem. methods with a high yield, and (b) it is highly hydrophilic and can form stable aq. colloids to facilitate the assembly of macroscopic structures by simple and cheap soln. processes, both of which are important to the large-scale uses of graphene.  A key topic in the research and applications of GO is the redn., which partly restores the structure and properties of graphene.  Different redn. processes result in different properties of reduced GO (rGO), which in turn affect the final performance of materials or devices composed of rGO.  In this contribution, the authors review the state-of-art status of the redn. of GO on both techniques and mechanisms.  The development in this field will speed the applications of graphene.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoYPzqnW5KjR7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgRVT8s4wfpWQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38Xms1ertLw%253D&amp;md5=ef65d8d276335b8681fc3d9616726bf2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1016/j.tsf.2007.07.187"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sano, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ying, W.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen and phosphorus dual-doped graphene/carbon nanosheets as bifunctional electrocatalysts for oxygen redn. and evolution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Rong; Wei, Zidong; Gou, Xinglong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Catalysis</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is highly desirable but challenging to develop bifunctional catalysts for efficiently catalyzing both the oxygen redn. reaction (ORR) and oxygen evolution reaction (OER) in energy storage and conversion systems.  Here a simple yet cost-effective strategy is developed to fabricate nitrogen and phosphorus dual-doped graphene/carbon nanosheets (N,P-GCNS) with N,P-doped carbon sandwiching few-layers-thick graphene.  The as-prepd. N,P-GCNS shows outstanding catalytic activity toward both ORR and OER with a potential gap of 0.71 V between the OER potential at a c.d. of 10 mA cm-2 and the ORR potential at a c.d. of -3 mA cm-2, illustrating that it is the best metal-free bifunctional electrocatalysts reported to date.  The superb bifunctional catalytic performance is attributed to the synergistic effects between the doped N and P atoms, the full exposure of the active sites on the surface of the N,P-GCNS nanosheets, the high cond. of the incorporated graphene, and the large surface area and hierarchical pores for sufficient contact and rapid transportation of the reactants.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIKCGk1OZwJbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgRVT8s4wfpWQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tunable and weakly negative permittivity in carbon/silicon nitride composites with different carbonizing temperatures</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Chuanbing; Fan, Runhua; Wang, Zhongyang; Shao, Qian; Guo, Xingkui; Xie, Peitao; Yin, Yansheng; Zhang, Yuliang; An, Liqiong; Lei, Yanhua; Ryu, Jong Eun; Shankar, Akash; Guo, Zhanhu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite the exotic electromagnetic properties have been demonstrated in metamaterials to date, how to effectively adjust neg. electromagnetic parameters remains a challenge.  Tunable neg. permittivity is essential for the metamaterials to satisfy a variety of practical applications, such as capacitor, microwave absorbing and shielding.  Here, we fabricated a random metamaterial, carbon/silicon nitride (C/Si3N4) composite, using a feasible impregnation-pyrolysis method.  The microstructure and dielec. property of the composites with different heat treatment temps. (HTTs) and carbon contents were investigated.  The amorphous carbon membrane adhered on the rod-like Si3N4 grains.  The neg. permittivity behavior combined with inductive character was obtained in the composites, which was attributed to the low frequency plasmonic state generated from the formative conducting carbon networks.  The magnitude of neg. permittivity is demonstrated to be successfully adjusted by controlling the HTT and carbon content.  The result is in good agreement with the anal. of Drude model.  Interestingly, a weakly neg. permittivity behavior was obsd. in the measured frequency, showing small neg. values of permittivity between -50 and -10, which was ascribed to a moderate carrier concn. provided by the carbon networks.  This work provides an effective way to achieve the tunable and weakly neg. permittivity in random metamaterials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrJvO-tQUJvkrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgRVT8s4wfpWQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsFCqsLrE&amp;md5=82dac524992545ccd8a25e431b8be103</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201209689"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Capacity and Rate Capability of Amorphous Phosphorus for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.
